          <div id="First_Macedonian_War" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em">
           <span style="line-height:1.6em">
            <a href="/wiki/First_Macedonian_War" title="First Macedonian War">
             <span class="wrap">
              First Macedonian War
             </span>
            </a>
           </span>
          </div>
         </th>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
          <div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
           <ul>
            <li>
             <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_Lamia" title="First Battle of Lamia">
              1st Lamia
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Lamia" title="Second Battle of Lamia">
              2nd Lamia
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mantinea_(207_BC)" title="Battle of Mantinea (207 BC)">
              Mantinea
             </a>
            </li>
           </ul>
          </div>
         </td>
        </tr>
       </table>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Second Punic War
       </b>
       , also referred to as
       <b>
        The Hannibalic War
       </b>
       and (by the Romans) the
       <b>
        War Against Hannibal
       </b>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       was a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_war" title="Global war">
        global war
       </a>
       that lasted from 218 to 201 BC
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and involved
       <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">
        great powers
       </a>
       in the western and eastern
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean" title="Mediterranean">
        Mediterranean
       </a>
       . It was the second major war between
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Carthage" title="Ancient Carthage">
        Carthage
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">
        Roman Republic
       </a>
       and its allied Italic
       <a href="/wiki/Socii" title="Socii">
        socii
       </a>
       , with the participation of
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">
        Greek
       </a>
       polities and
       <a href="/wiki/Numidians" title="Numidians">
        Numidian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">
        Iberian
       </a>
       forces on both sides.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Second Punic War is one of the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_wars_and_anthropogenic_disasters_by_death_toll" title="List of wars and anthropogenic disasters by death toll">
        deadliest human conflicts
       </a>
       in ancient times. Regarded by ancient historians as the greatest war in history, waged with unparalleled resources, skill and hatred,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livy_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Livy-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/10907/10907-h/10907-h.htm#c1" rel="nofollow">
          21.1
         </a>
        </span>
       </sup>
       it saw hundreds of thousands killed, some of the most
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_battles_by_casualties" title="List of battles by casualties">
        lethal battles
       </a>
       in military history, the destruction of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cities" title="Cities">
        cities
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Massacre" title="Massacre">
        massacres
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">
        enslavements
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Civilian" title="Civilian">
        civilian
       </a>
       populations and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prisoners_of_war" title="Prisoners of war">
        prisoners of war
       </a>
       by both sides.
      </p>
      <p>
       The war began with the Carthaginian
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_(military)" title="General (military)">
        general
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Hannibal" title="Hannibal">
        Hannibal
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Saguntum" title="Siege of Saguntum">
        conquest
       </a>
       and destruction of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">
        Roman
       </a>
       -allied
       <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">
        Iberian
       </a>
       city of
       <a href="/wiki/Sagunto_Castle" title="Sagunto Castle">
        Saguntum
       </a>
       in 219 BC, prompting a Roman declaration of war on Carthage in 218. Hannibal surprised the Romans by marching his
       <a href="/wiki/Army" title="Army">
        army
       </a>
       overland from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iberia" title="Iberia">
        Iberia
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Hannibal%27s_crossing_of_the_Alps" title="Hannibal's crossing of the Alps">
        cross the Alps
       </a>
       and invade
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Italy" title="Roman Italy">
        Roman Italy
       </a>
       , followed by his reinforcement by
       <a href="/wiki/Gauls" title="Gauls">
        Gallic
       </a>
       allies and crushing victories over Roman armies at
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Trebia" title="Battle of the Trebia">
        Trebia river
       </a>
       in 218 and on the shores of
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lake_Trasimene" title="Battle of Lake Trasimene">
        Lake Trasimene
       </a>
       in 217. Moving to
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Italy" title="Southern Italy">
        southern Italy
       </a>
       in 216, Hannibal at
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cannae" title="Battle of Cannae">
        Cannae
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_annihilation" title="Battle of annihilation">
        annihilated
       </a>
       the largest army the Romans had ever assembled, killing or capturing more than 67,000 Roman soldiers. After the death or imprisonment of 130,000 Roman troops in two years, 40% of Rome's
       <a href="/wiki/Socii" title="Socii">
        Italian allies
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Defection" title="Defection">
        defected
       </a>
       to Carthage, giving her control over most of southern Italy.
       <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(ancient_kingdom)" title="Macedonia (ancient kingdom)">
        Macedon
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Syracuse" title="Kingdom of Syracuse">
        Syracuse
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/First_Macedonian_War" title="First Macedonian War">
        joined
       </a>
       the Carthaginian side after Cannae and the conflict spread to
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">
        Greece
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">
        Sicily
       </a>
       . The Carthaginian
       <a href="/wiki/Navy" title="Navy">
        navy
       </a>
       was built up in the early years of the war and from 215–210, the
       <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Carthage" title="Military of Carthage">
        Carthaginian army
       </a>
       and navy launched
       <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_warfare" title="Amphibious warfare">
        amphibious
       </a>
       assaults to capture Roman Sicily and
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Decimomannu" title="Battle of Decimomannu">
        Sardinia
       </a>
       but were ultimately repulsed.
      </p>
      <p>
       Against Hannibal's skill on the battlefield, the Romans adopted the
       <a href="/wiki/Fabian_strategy" title="Fabian strategy">
        Fabian strategy
       </a>
       - the avoidance of battle against Hannibal and defeating his allies and the other Carthaginian generals instead. Roman armies recaptured all of the great cities that had joined Carthage and defeated a Carthaginian attempt to reinforce Hannibal at
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Metaurus" title="Battle of the Metaurus">
        Metaurus
       </a>
       in 207. Southern Italy was turned into a wasteland by the combatants, with hundreds of thousands of civilians killed or enslaved. In Iberia, which served as a major source of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manpower" title="Manpower">
        manpower
       </a>
       for the Carthaginian army, a Roman
       <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Expeditionary_force" title="Expeditionary force">
        expeditionary force
       </a>
       under
       <a href="/wiki/Scipio_Africanus" title="Scipio Africanus">
        Publius Cornelius Scipio
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cartagena_(209_BC)" title="Battle of Cartagena (209 BC)">
        captured
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Spain" title="Cartagena, Spain">
        Carthago Nova
       </a>
       , Carthage's
       <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">
        capital city
       </a>
       in Iberia, in 209, massacring and enslaving the inhabitants. Scipio's destruction of a Carthaginian army at
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ilipa" title="Battle of Ilipa">
        Ilipa
       </a>
       in 206 permanently ended
       <a href="/wiki/Carthaginian_Iberia" title="Carthaginian Iberia">
        Carthaginian rule
       </a>
       in Iberia. He invaded Carthaginian
       <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">
        Africa
       </a>
       in 204, inflicting two severe defeats on Carthage and her allies at
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Utica_(203_BC)" title="Battle of Utica (203 BC)">
        Utica
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Great_Plains" title="Battle of the Great Plains">
        Great Plains
       </a>
       that compelled the Carthaginian
       <a href="/wiki/Senate" title="Senate">
        senate
       </a>
       to recall Hannibal's army from Italy. The final engagement between Scipio and Hannibal took place at
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Zama" title="Battle of Zama">
        Zama
       </a>
       in Africa in 202 and resulted in Hannibal's defeat and the imposition of harsh peace conditions on Carthage (
       <a href="/wiki/Carthaginian_peace" title="Carthaginian peace">
        Carthaginian peace
       </a>
       ), which ceased to be a great power and became a Roman
       <a href="/wiki/Client_state" title="Client state">
        client state
       </a>
       until its
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Carthage_(c._149_BC)" title="Battle of Carthage (c. 149 BC)">
        final destruction
       </a>
       by the Romans in 146 BC during the
       <a href="/wiki/Third_Punic_War" title="Third Punic War">
        Third Punic War
       </a>
       . The Second Punic War overthrew the established
       <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Balance_of_power" title="Balance of power">
        balance of power
       </a>
       of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_world" title="Ancient world">
        ancient world
       </a>
       and Rome rose to become the dominant power in the
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">
        Mediterranean Basin
       </a>
       for the next 600 years.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

             11.3
            </span>
            <span class="toctext">
             Secondary sources
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41">
         <a href="#External_links">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           12
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           External links
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
      </div>
      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Background">
        Background
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       For an analysis of the strength and organisation of Roman forces on the eve of the war, see
       <a href="/wiki/Socii#Military_organisation_of_the_Roman_alliance" title="Socii">
        Socii § Military organisation of the Roman alliance
       </a>
       .
      </div>
      <p>
       The Second Punic War was fought between Carthage and Rome. The war was ignited by the dispute over the
       <a href="/wiki/Hegemony" title="Hegemony">
        hegemony
       </a>
       of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saguntum" title="Saguntum">
        Saguntum
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Hellenization" title="Hellenization">
        Hellenized
       </a>
       Iberian coastal city with diplomatic contacts with Rome.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mahaney2008_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mahaney2008-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After great tension within the city government, culminating in the assassination of the supporters of Carthage, Hannibal laid
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Saguntum" title="Siege of Saguntum">
        siege to the city of Saguntum
       </a>
       in 219 BC. The city called for Roman aid, but the pleas fell on deaf ears. Following a prolonged
       <a href="/wiki/Siege" title="Siege">
        siege
       </a>
       and a bloody struggle, in which Hannibal himself was wounded and the army practically destroyed, the Carthaginians finally took control of the city. Many of the Saguntians chose to commit suicide rather than face subjugation by the Carthaginians.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011230_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011230-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Before the war, Rome and
       <a href="/wiki/Hasdrubal_the_Fair" title="Hasdrubal the Fair">
        Hasdrubal the Fair
       </a>
       had made a treaty.
       <a href="/wiki/Livy" title="Livy">
        Livy
       </a>
       reports that it was agreed that the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iber" title="Iber">
        Iber
       </a>
       should be the boundary between the two empires and that the liberty of the Saguntines should be preserved.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livy_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Livy-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/10907/10907-h/10907-h.htm#c8" rel="nofollow">
          21.13
         </a>
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span id="Hannibal_takes_the_initiative_.28218.E2.80.93213_BC.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hannibal_takes_the_initiative_(218–213_BC)">
        Hannibal takes the initiative (218–213 BC)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Hannibal takes the initiative (218–213 BC)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span id="Western_Mediterranean_.28218.E2.80.93213_BC.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Western_Mediterranean_(218–213_BC)">
        Western Mediterranean (218–213 BC)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Western Mediterranean (218–213 BC)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span id="Hannibal.27s_Overland_Journey">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hannibal's_Overland_Journey">
        Hannibal's Overland Journey
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Hannibal's Overland Journey">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hannibal_route_of_invasion-en.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="479" data-file-width="764" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Hannibal_route_of_invasion-en.svg/300px-Hannibal_route_of_invasion-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Hannibal_route_of_invasion-en.svg/450px-Hannibal_route_of_invasion-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Hannibal_route_of_invasion-en.svg/600px-Hannibal_route_of_invasion-en.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hannibal_route_of_invasion-en.svg" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         Route of Hannibal's invasion of Italy
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hannibal_traversant_les_Alpes_%C3%A0_dos_d%27%C3%A9l%C3%A9phant_-_Nicolas_Poussin.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="2500" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Hannibal_traversant_les_Alpes_%C3%A0_dos_d%27%C3%A9l%C3%A9phant_-_Nicolas_Poussin.jpg/220px-Hannibal_traversant_les_Alpes_%C3%A0_dos_d%27%C3%A9l%C3%A9phant_-_Nicolas_Poussin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Hannibal_traversant_les_Alpes_%C3%A0_dos_d%27%C3%A9l%C3%A9phant_-_Nicolas_Poussin.jpg/330px-Hannibal_traversant_les_Alpes_%C3%A0_dos_d%27%C3%A9l%C3%A9phant_-_Nicolas_Poussin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Hannibal_traversant_les_Alpes_%C3%A0_dos_d%27%C3%A9l%C3%A9phant_-_Nicolas_Poussin.jpg/440px-Hannibal_traversant_les_Alpes_%C3%A0_dos_d%27%C3%A9l%C3%A9phant_-_Nicolas_Poussin.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hannibal_traversant_les_Alpes_%C3%A0_dos_d%27%C3%A9l%C3%A9phant_-_Nicolas_Poussin.jpg" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         Hannibal won fame for trekking across the Alps with 37 war elephants. His surprise tactics and brilliant strategies put Rome against the ropes.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Carthaginian army in Iberia, excluding the forces in Africa, according to
       <a href="/wiki/Polybius" title="Polybius">
        Polybius
       </a>
       , totalled 90,000
       <a href="/wiki/Infantry" title="Infantry">
        infantry
       </a>
       , 12,000
       <a href="/wiki/Cavalry" title="Cavalry">
        cavalry
       </a>
       , and 37
       <a href="/wiki/War_elephant" title="War elephant">
        war elephants
       </a>
       :
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       it was thus one of the largest in the Hellenistic world and equal in numbers to any that the Romans had yet fielded. Hannibal departed with this army from New Carthage (
       <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Spain" title="Cartagena, Spain">
        Cartagena, Spain
       </a>
       ) northwards along the coast in late spring of 218 BC. At the
       <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">
        Ebro
       </a>
       , he split the army into three columns and subdued the tribes from there to the
       <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">
        Pyrenees
       </a>
       within weeks, but with severe losses. At the Pyrenees, he left a detachment of 11,000 Iberian troops, who showed reluctance to leave their homeland, as a garrison for the newly conquered region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Hannibal reportedly entered
       <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">
        Gaul
       </a>
       with 50,000 infantry and 9,000 cavalry. He took his army by an inland route,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mahaney2008_4-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mahaney2008-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       avoiding the Roman allies along the coast. In Gaul, negotiations helped him to move unmolested except for the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Rhone_Crossing" title="Battle of Rhone Crossing">
        Battle of Rhone Crossing
       </a>
       , where a force of the
       <a href="/wiki/Allobroges" title="Allobroges">
        Allobroges
       </a>
       unsuccessfully tried to oppose his 38,000 infantry (this number may exclude light infantry), 8,000 cavalry, and 37 war elephants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the meantime, a Roman fleet with an invasion force was underway to northern Iberia. Its commanders, the brothers
       <a href="/wiki/Gnaeus_Cornelius_Scipio_Calvus" title="Gnaeus Cornelius Scipio Calvus">
        Gnaeus Cornelius Scipio Calvus
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Publius_Cornelius_Scipio" title="Publius Cornelius Scipio">
        Publius Cornelius Scipio
       </a>
       , knew that Hannibal had crossed the Ebro, but were surprised by the Carthaginian army's presence at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhone" title="Rhone">
        Rhone
       </a>
       upstream of their ally
       <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">
        Massalia
       </a>
       , where they had landed. A scouting party of 300 cavalry was sent to discover the whereabouts of the enemy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mahaney2008_4-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-mahaney2008-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These eventually defeated a Carthaginian scouting troop of 500 mounted Numidians and chased them back to their main camp. Thus, with knowledge of the location of the enemy, the Romans marched upstream, ready for battle. Hannibal evaded this force and by an unknown route reached the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Is%C3%A8re_River" title="Isère River">
        Isère
       </a>
       or the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Durance_River" title="Durance River">
        Durance
       </a>
       at the foot of the Alps in autumn.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mahaney2008_4-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-mahaney2008-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He also received messengers from his Gallic allies in Italy that urged him to come to their aid and offered to guide him over the Alps. Before setting out to cross the Alps, he was re-supplied by a native tribe, some of whose hereditary disputes he had helped solve.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="First_Roman_expedition_to_Iberia">
        First Roman expedition to Iberia
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: First Roman expedition to Iberia">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Relieve_de_Osuna_(M.A.N._Madrid)_03.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1519" data-file-width="1242" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Relieve_de_Osuna_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_03.jpg/200px-Relieve_de_Osuna_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Relieve_de_Osuna_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_03.jpg/300px-Relieve_de_Osuna_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Relieve_de_Osuna_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_03.jpg/400px-Relieve_de_Osuna_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_03.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Relieve_de_Osuna_(M.A.N._Madrid)_03.jpg" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         Iberian warrior from bas-relief c. 200 BC. The warrior is armed with a
         <a href="/wiki/Falcata" title="Falcata">
          falcata
         </a>
         and an oval shield.
         <a href="/wiki/National_Archaeological_Museum_of_Spain" title="National Archaeological Museum of Spain">
          National Archaeological Museum of Spain
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">
          Madrid
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Falcata_%C3%ADbera_(M.A.N._Madrid)_03.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="416" data-file-width="2723" height="31" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Falcata_%C3%ADbera_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_03.jpg/200px-Falcata_%C3%ADbera_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Falcata_%C3%ADbera_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_03.jpg/300px-Falcata_%C3%ADbera_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Falcata_%C3%ADbera_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_03.jpg/400px-Falcata_%C3%ADbera_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_03.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Falcata_%C3%ADbera_(M.A.N._Madrid)_03.jpg" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         Iberian
         <a href="/wiki/Falcata" title="Falcata">
          falcata
         </a>
         , 4th/3rd century BC. This weapon, a scythe-shaped sword, was unique to Iberia
         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
          [
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
            <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2015)">
             citation needed
            </span>
           </a>
          </i>
          ]
         </sup>
         . By its inherent weight distribution, it could deliver blows as powerful as an axe. National Archaeological Museum of Spain, Madrid
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dishekel_hispano-cartagin%C3%A9s-2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="196" data-file-width="422" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Dishekel_hispano-cartagin%C3%A9s-2.jpg/300px-Dishekel_hispano-cartagin%C3%A9s-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f0/Dishekel_hispano-cartagin%C3%A9s-2.jpg 1.5x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dishekel_hispano-cartagin%C3%A9s-2.jpg" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a href="/wiki/Carthaginian_currency" title="Carthaginian currency">
          Carthaginian
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Shekel" title="Shekel">
          shekel
         </a>
         , dated 237-227 BC, depicting the Punic god
         <a href="/wiki/Melqart" title="Melqart">
          Melqart
         </a>
         (equivalent of
         <a href="/wiki/Hercules" title="Hercules">
          Hercules
         </a>
         /
         <a href="/wiki/Heracles" title="Heracles">
          Heracles
         </a>
         ), most likely with the features of
         <a href="/wiki/Hamilcar_Barca" title="Hamilcar Barca">
          Hamilcar Barca
         </a>
         , father of
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hannibal_Barca" title="Hannibal Barca">
          Hannibal Barca
         </a>
         ; on the reverse is a man riding a
         <a href="/wiki/War_elephant" title="War elephant">
          war elephant
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The first Roman expedition to Iberia was unable to bring the Carthaginian troops in the hinterland of
       <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">
        Massalia
       </a>
       to a
       <a href="/wiki/Pitched_battle" title="Pitched battle">
        pitched battle
       </a>
       , so it continued on its way to northern Iberia under
       <a href="/wiki/Gnaeus_Cornelius_Scipio_Calvus" title="Gnaeus Cornelius Scipio Calvus">
        Gnaeus Cornelius Scipio Calvus
       </a>
       , a move which proved decisive for the outcome of the war. Their other commander,
       <a href="/wiki/Publius_Cornelius_Scipio" title="Publius Cornelius Scipio">
        Publius Cornelius Scipio
       </a>
       , returned to Rome, realizing the danger of an invasion of Italy where the tribes of the
       <a href="/wiki/Boii" title="Boii">
        Boii
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Insubres" title="Insubres">
        Insubres
       </a>
       were already in revolt. After 217 BC, he moved to Iberia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011321_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011321-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In Iberia, Carthaginian rule was not popular, but Roman inaction during the
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Saguntum" title="Siege of Saguntum">
        Siege of Saguntum
       </a>
       had made the natives cautious about an alliance against their masters. Gnaeus Cornelius Scipio Calvus established his headquarters at
       <a href="/wiki/Tarraco" title="Tarraco">
        Cissa
       </a>
       , in the midst of Hannibal's latest acquisition, the area between Ebro and Pyrenees. Despite initial setbacks, he won increasing support among the natives. This convinced the Carthaginian commander
       <a href="/wiki/Hanno,_son_of_Bomilcar" title="Hanno, son of Bomilcar">
        Hanno
       </a>
       , the nephew of Hannibal, of the necessity to accept pitched battle before his troops had been united with the army under
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hasdrubal_(Barcid)" title="Hasdrubal (Barcid)">
        Hasdrubal
       </a>
       , the brother of Hannibal, despite being outnumbered 2 to 1. The result was a Roman victory in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cissa" title="Battle of Cissa">
        Battle of Cissa
       </a>
       in 218 BC. When Hasdrubal finally made it to the scene, he was in no position to fight the Roman army and merely caught their navy personnel off-guard, killing some in the process.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011321_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011321-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The combined Roman and
       <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">
        Massalian
       </a>
       fleet and army posed a threat to the Carthaginians. Hasdrubal intended to first defeat the fleet. However, his naval forces had a history of failure against the Romans. They had lost all but one major naval engagement in the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Punic_War" title="First Punic War">
        First Punic War
       </a>
       and in 218 BC a naval engagement in the waters of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lilybaeum" title="Lilybaeum">
        Lilybaeum
       </a>
       had been lost despite numerical superiority. For this reason, he moved the army and fleet in unison. The fleet is described as being very disorganized prior to the battle. The army, in the meantime, provided loud moral support and a safe harbour for the ensuing naval
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ebro_River" title="Battle of Ebro River">
        Battle of Ebro River
       </a>
       . The 40 Carthaginian and Iberian vessels were severely defeated by the 55 Roman and Massalian ships in the second naval engagement of the war, with about three quarters of the Carthaginian fleet captured or sunk and the rest beaching their ships. In the aftermath, the Carthaginian forces retreated, but the Romans were still confined to the area between Ebro and Pyrenees.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011321_9-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011321-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       This blocking force of Romans prevented the Carthaginians from sending reinforcements from Iberia to Hannibal or to the insurgent Gauls in northern Italy during critical stages of the war. Hasdrubal acted by marching into Roman territory in 215 BC and offered
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dertosa" title="Battle of Dertosa">
        battle at Dertosa
       </a>
       . In this battle, he used his cavalry superiority to clear the field and to envelop the enemy on both sides with his infantry, a tactic that had been very successfully employed in Italy. However, the Romans broke through the thinned-out line in the centre and defeated both wings separately, inflicting severe losses, but not without taking heavy losses themselves.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011322_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011322-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       While the Romans made little progress in the Iberian theatre, the Scipios were able to negotiate a new front in Africa by allying themselves with
       <a href="/wiki/Syphax" title="Syphax">
        Syphax
       </a>
       , a powerful
       <a href="/wiki/Numidians" title="Numidians">
        Numidian
       </a>
       king in North Africa. In 213 BC, he received Roman advisers to train his heavy infantry soldiers that had not yet been able to stand up to their Carthaginian counterparts. With this support, he waged war against the Carthaginian ally
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Kings_of_Numidia#Kings_of_Eastern_Numidia" title="List of Kings of Numidia">
        Gala
       </a>
       . According to
       <a href="/wiki/Appian" title="Appian">
        Appian
       </a>
       , in 213 BC
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hasdrubal_(Barcid)" title="Hasdrubal (Barcid)">
        Hasdrubal
       </a>
       left Iberia and fought Syphax, though history may have confused him with
       <a href="/wiki/Hasdrubal_Gisco" title="Hasdrubal Gisco">
        Hasdrubal Gisco
       </a>
       ; however, it did use Carthaginian resources.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Hasdrubal Gisco is the son of the Gesco who had served together with
       <a href="/wiki/Hamilcar_Barca" title="Hamilcar Barca">
        Hamilcar Barca
       </a>
       , Hannibal's father, in Sicily during the First Punic War and son-in-law of
       <a href="/wiki/Hanno_the_Elder" title="Hanno the Elder">
        Hanno the Elder
       </a>
       who was one of Hannibal's lieutenants in Italy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011322_10-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011322-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Central_Mediterranean_.28218.E2.80.93213_BC.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Central_Mediterranean_(218–213_BC)">
        Central Mediterranean (218–213 BC)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Central Mediterranean (218–213 BC)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Naval_raids_and_expeditions">
        Naval raids and expeditions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Naval raids and expeditions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       In 218 BC, the Carthaginian navy was scouting
       <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">
        Sicilian
       </a>
       waters and preparing for a surprise attack on their former key stronghold of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lilybaeum" title="Lilybaeum">
        Lilybaeum
       </a>
       on the western tip of the island. Twenty
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quinquereme" title="Quinquereme">
        quinqueremes
       </a>
       , loaded with 1,000 soldiers, raided the
       <a href="/wiki/Aegadian_Islands" title="Aegadian Islands">
        Aegadian Islands
       </a>
       west of Sicily and eight ships intended to attack the
       <a href="/wiki/Aeolian_Islands" title="Aeolian Islands">
        Aeolian Islands
       </a>
       , but were blown off-course in a storm towards the Straits of Messina. The Syracusan navy, then at Messina, captured three of those without resistance. Learning from their crews that a Carthaginian fleet was to attack Lilybaeum,
       <a href="/wiki/Hiero_II_of_Syracuse" title="Hiero II of Syracuse">
        Hiero II
       </a>
       warned the Roman
       <a href="/wiki/Praetor" title="Praetor">
        praetor
       </a>
       Marcus Amellius there. As a result, the Romans prepared 20
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quinquereme" title="Quinquereme">
        quinqueremes
       </a>
       to intercept, and defeated the 35 Carthaginian quinqueremes in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lilybaeum" title="Battle of Lilybaeum">
        Battle of Lilybaeum
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 218 BC, preparations were made to launch a Roman expedition from Lilybaeum against Africa. Hannibal had anticipated the move and reinforced the defending army in Africa with 13,850 Iberian heavy infantry, 870 Balearic slingers and 1,200 Iberian cavalry. In addition, some 4,000 Iberian men "of good family were called up who were under orders to be conveyed to Carthage to strengthen its defence, and also to serve as hostages for the loyalty of their people."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livy_3-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Livy-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/10907/10907-h/10907-h.htm#c21" rel="nofollow">
          21.21
         </a>
        </span>
       </sup>
       In return, 11,850
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Libya" title="Ancient Libya">
        Libyan
       </a>
       infantry, 300
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ligurians" title="Ligurians">
        Ligurians
       </a>
       , and 500 Balearic slingers were sent to Iberia to strengthen the local defence against the other anticipated Roman invasion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livy_3-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Livy-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/10907/10907-h/10907-h.htm#c22" rel="nofollow">
          21.22
         </a>
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Carthaginian navy had been defeated by the Romans in two major encounters, but neither side was usually able to stop the other from raiding each other's coasts. An exception was in 217 BC, when a Carthaginian fleet of 70 quinqueremes was intercepted off the coast of
       <a href="/wiki/Etruria" title="Etruria">
        Etruria
       </a>
       by a Roman fleet of 120 quinqueremes and retreated without giving battle.
      </p>
      <p>
       The first Carthaginian expedition to
       <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">
        Sardinia
       </a>
       , in 215 BC, was under the command of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hasdrubal_The_Bald" title="Hasdrubal The Bald">
        Hasdrubal The Bald
       </a>
       with his Punic-Sardinian subordinate
       <a href="/wiki/Hampsicora" title="Hampsicora">
        Hampsicora
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011365_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011365-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A previous pro-Carthaginian uprising had been defeated, while a storm had blown the Carthaginian fleet to the
       <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">
        Balearic Islands
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livy_3-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Livy-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/10907/10907-h/10907-h.htm#e34" rel="nofollow">
          23.24
         </a>
        </span>
       </sup>
       When they finally arrived at Sardinia, the Romans were aware of their intentions and had reinforced the unpopular garrison under
       <a href="/wiki/Titus_Manlius_Torquatus_(dictator)" title="Titus Manlius Torquatus (dictator)">
        Titus Manlius Torquatus
       </a>
       to 20,000 infantry and 1,200 cavalry. These engaged and defeated the Carthaginians' 12,000 infantry and 1,500 cavalry (plus an unknown number of elephants) and the remaining insurgent Sardinians at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cornus" title="Battle of Cornus">
        Battle of Cornus
       </a>
       . In the aftermath, the defeated expedition of 60 quinqueremes and several transports encountered a Roman raiding party from Africa with 100 quinqueremes. The Carthaginian fleet scattered and escaped save for seven ships. As a result, Sardinia, an important grain exporter, remained under Roman occupation.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Gallic_uprising">
        Gallic uprising
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Gallic uprising">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The Romans simultaneously received news of Hannibal's crossing of the Ebro and of an uprising in northern Italy of the Gallic tribes
       <a href="/wiki/Boii" title="Boii">
        Boii
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Insubres" title="Insubres">
        Insubres
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livy_3-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-Livy-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/10907/10907-h/10907-h.htm#c25" rel="nofollow">
          21.25
         </a>
        </span>
       </sup>
       These had established diplomatic contact with the Carthaginians and joined them as allies against their common enemy, Rome. The first objective of the insurgents were the Roman colonies of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Placentia,_Italy" title="Placentia, Italy">
        Placentia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cremona" title="Cremona">
        Cremona
       </a>
       , causing the Romans to flee to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mutina" title="Mutina">
        Mutina
       </a>
       (modern Modena), which the Gauls then besieged. In response,
       <a href="/wiki/Praetor" title="Praetor">
        Praetor
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L._Manlius_Vulso" title="L. Manlius Vulso">
        L. Manlius Vulso
       </a>
       marched with two
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_legion" title="Roman legion">
        legions
       </a>
       and allies, for a total of 1,600 cavalry and 20,000 infantry, to
       <a href="/wiki/Cisalpine_Gaul" title="Cisalpine Gaul">
        Cisalpine Gaul
       </a>
       . This army was ambushed twice on the way from
       <a href="/wiki/Rimini" title="Rimini">
        Ariminium
       </a>
       , losing 1,200 men; although the siege of Mutina was raised, the army itself fell under a loose siege a few kilometers from Mutina.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This event prompted the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Senate" title="Roman Senate">
        Roman Senate
       </a>
       to send one of Scipio's legions and 5,000 allied troops to aid Vulso. Scipio had to raise fresh troops to replace these and thus could not set out for Iberia until September 218 BC, giving Hannibal time to march from the Ebro to the Rhone.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011283_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011283-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After evading a pitched battle at the Rhone, Hannibal came to the aid of his Gallic allies, who were hard pressed by the Roman reinforcements. He crossed the Alps, surmounting the difficulties of climate and terrain,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mahaney2008_4-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-mahaney2008-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">
        guerrilla tactics
       </a>
       of the native tribes. His exact route is disputed. Hannibal arrived with at least 28,000 infantry, 6,000 cavalry, and 30 elephants in the territory of the
       <a href="/wiki/Taurini" title="Taurini">
        Taurini
       </a>
       , in what is now
       <a href="/wiki/Piedmont" title="Piedmont">
        Piedmont
       </a>
       , northern Italy. While this crossing was expected by the Romans, they had not anticipated such an early arrival and their forces were still in their winter quarters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livy_3-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-Livy-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/10907/10907-h/10907-h.htm#c32" rel="nofollow">
          21.32–38
         </a>
        </span>
       </sup>
       Hannibal's crossing of the Alps is considered one of the greatest achievements in military logistics, as he did so through hostile territory in late autumn with no supply line. His surprise entry into the Italian peninsula led to the termination of Rome's main intended thrust, an invasion of Africa.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011283_14-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011283-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Gauls of the lower
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Po_River" title="Po River">
        Po Valley
       </a>
       , Hannibal's allies, were still far away. Hannibal was first obliged to fight with his currently reduced force to reach them and incite the rest of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallia_Cisalpina" title="Gallia Cisalpina">
        Gallia Cisalpina
       </a>
       to revolt. His first action was to take the chief city of the hostile
       <a href="/wiki/Taurini" title="Taurini">
        Taurini
       </a>
       (in the area of modern-day Turin). Afterwards, the Carthaginians were intercepted by a newly raised Roman force under
       <a href="/wiki/Publius_Cornelius_Scipio" title="Publius Cornelius Scipio">
        Publius Cornelius Scipio
       </a>
       , who Hannibal had evaded earlier in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhone" title="Rhone">
        Rhone
       </a>
       Valley. In the ensuing
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ticinus" title="Battle of Ticinus">
        Battle of Ticinus
       </a>
       , the cavalry forces of Hannibal's army defeated the cavalry and light infantry of the Romans in a minor engagement. Scipio, severely injured in the battle, retreated across the
       <a href="/wiki/Trebbia" title="Trebbia">
        River Trebia
       </a>
       with his heavy infantry still intact, and encamped at the town of
       <a href="/wiki/Piacenza" title="Piacenza">
        Placentia
       </a>
       to await reinforcements. As a result of Rome's defeat at the Ticinus, all the Gauls except the
       <a href="/wiki/Cenomani" title="Cenomani">
        Cenomani
       </a>
       were induced to join the Carthaginian cause. Soon, the entire north of Italy was unofficially insurgent, with both Gallic and Ligurian troops bolstering Hannibal's army to at least 40,000 men.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011284_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011284-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_trebia-en.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="740" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Battle_trebia-en.png/300px-Battle_trebia-en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Battle_trebia-en.png/450px-Battle_trebia-en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Battle_trebia-en.png/600px-Battle_trebia-en.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_trebia-en.png" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Trebia" title="Battle of the Trebia">
          Battle of the Trebia
         </a>
         plan.
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000088; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Carthaginians
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ee0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Romans
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Even before news of the defeat at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ticino_River" title="Ticino River">
        Ticinus River
       </a>
       had reached Rome, the Senate had ordered the consul
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sempronius_Longus" title="Sempronius Longus">
        Sempronius Longus
       </a>
       to bring his army back from Sicily, where it had been preparing for the invasion of Africa, to join Scipio and face Hannibal. Hannibal was blocking Sempronius' way to Scipio's army. However, the Carthaginian capture of the supply depot at
       <a href="/wiki/Clastidium" title="Clastidium">
        Clastidium
       </a>
       , through the treachery of the local
       <a href="/wiki/Latins" title="Latins">
        Latin
       </a>
       commander, served as a diversion and allowed Sempronius' army to slip through to Scipio, who was still too seriously injured to take the field. After some minor successes, the united and numerically equal Roman force under the command of Sempronius Longus was lured into combat by Hannibal at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Trebia" title="Battle of the Trebia">
        battle of the Trebia
       </a>
       . The Roman troops were drawn into the engagement without breakfast and first had to cross a cold river, preventing many from putting up much of a fight. Furthermore, a hidden detachment led by Hannibal's younger brother
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mago_(Barcid)" title="Mago (Barcid)">
        Mago
       </a>
       attacked them from the rear. All in all, the Romans suffered heavy losses with only 20,000 men out of 40,000 able to retreat to safety. They left Cisalpine Gaul in the aftermath. Having secured his position in northern Italy by this victory, Hannibal quartered his troops for the winter amongst the Gauls. The latter joined his army in large numbers, bringing it up to 60,000 men; their enthusiasm was somewhat reduced due to the Carthaginians living on their land.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011284_15-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011284-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Roman Senate resolved to raise new armies against Hannibal under the recently elected consuls of 217 BC,
       <a href="/wiki/Gnaeus_Servilius_Geminus" title="Gnaeus Servilius Geminus">
        Gnaeus Servilius Geminus
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Gaius_Flaminius" title="Gaius Flaminius">
        Gaius Flaminius
       </a>
       . The latter had long distrusted his fellow senators and feared that they would try to sabotage his command by finding excuses to delay his departure. So he quietly left Rome to take over his army at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ariminum" title="Ariminum">
        Ariminum
       </a>
       without performing the lengthy religious rituals required of an incoming
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_consul" title="Roman consul">
        consul
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livy_3-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-Livy-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/10907/10907-h/10907-h.htm#c63" rel="nofollow">
          21.63
         </a>
        </span>
       </sup>
       The Senate voted unanimously to recall him, but he ignored its orders. This caused widespread dismay among the Romans, who feared that Flaminius' disrespect for the gods would bring disaster on Rome. As it was expected that Hannibal would advance into central Italy, Flaminius moved his army from Ariminum to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arretium" title="Arretium">
        Arretium
       </a>
       , to cover the
       <a href="/wiki/Apennine_Mountains" title="Apennine Mountains">
        Apennine
       </a>
       mountain passes into
       <a href="/wiki/Etruria" title="Etruria">
        Etruria
       </a>
       . His colleague Servilius, who had performed the proper rituals and was therefore well behind Flaminius, replaced him with his freshly raised army at Ariminum to cover the route along the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adriatic" title="Adriatic">
        Adriatic
       </a>
       coast. A third force, containing the survivors of previous engagements, was also stationed in Etruria under Scipio. Thus both the eastern and western routes to Rome appeared guarded.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011285_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011285-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_lake_trasimene.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="983" data-file-width="1280" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Battle_of_lake_trasimene.gif/300px-Battle_of_lake_trasimene.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Battle_of_lake_trasimene.gif/450px-Battle_of_lake_trasimene.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Battle_of_lake_trasimene.gif/600px-Battle_of_lake_trasimene.gif 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_lake_trasimene.gif" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lake_Trasimene" title="Battle of Lake Trasimene">
          Battle of Lake Trasimene
         </a>
         plan
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000088; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Carthaginians
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ee0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Romans
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In early spring 217 BC, Hannibal decided to advance, leaving his wavering Gallic allies in the Po Valley and crossed the
       <a href="/wiki/Apennine_Mountains" title="Apennine Mountains">
        Apennines
       </a>
       unopposed. He avoided the Roman positions and took the only unguarded route into
       <a href="/wiki/Etruria" title="Etruria">
        Etruria
       </a>
       at the mouth of the
       <a href="/wiki/Arno" title="Arno">
        Arno
       </a>
       . This route was through a huge marsh, which happened to be more flooded than usual for spring. Hannibal's army marched for several days without finding convenient places to rest, suffering terribly from fatigue and lack of sleep. This led to the loss of part of the force, including, it seems, the few remaining elephants.
      </p>
      <p>
       Arriving in Etruria, still in the spring of 217 BC, Hannibal tried without success to draw the main Roman army under Flaminius into a
       <a href="/wiki/Pitched_battle" title="Pitched battle">
        pitched battle
       </a>
       by devastating the area the latter had been sent to protect.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hart_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-hart-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Hannibal then employed a new
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/stratagem" title="wikt:stratagem">
        stratagem
       </a>
       , when he marched around his opponent’s left flank and effectively cut him off from Rome. Advancing through the uplands of Etruria, the Carthaginian now provoked Flaminius into a hasty pursuit without proper reconnaissance. Then, in a
       <a href="/wiki/Defile_(geography)" title="Defile (geography)">
        defile
       </a>
       on the shore of
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Trasimeno" title="Lake Trasimeno">
        Lake Trasimenus
       </a>
       , Hannibal lay in ambush with his army. The ambush was a complete success: in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lake_Trasimene" title="Battle of Lake Trasimene">
        battle of Lake Trasimene
       </a>
       Hannibal destroyed most of the Roman army and killed Flaminius with little loss to his own army. 6,000 Romans had been able to escape, but were caught and forced to surrender by
       <a href="/wiki/Maharbal" title="Maharbal">
        Maharbal
       </a>
       's Numidians. Furthermore, Scipio, aware of the fighting, sent his cavalry in support but it was also caught and annihilated. As a result of this victory, the heterogeneous force of insurgent Gauls, Africans, Iberians and Numidians had more military equipment than they could use themselves and sold the surplus via
       <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
        Egyptian
       </a>
       traders to the Romans. Like after all previous engagements, the captured enemies were sorted according to whether they were Romans, who were held captive, or non-Romans, who were released to spread the propaganda that the Carthaginian army was in Italy to fight for their freedom against the Romans. Strategically, Hannibal had now disposed of the only field force that could check his advance on Rome; but, despite the urgings of his generals, he did not proceed to attack Rome. Instead, he marched to the south in the hope of winning over allies amongst the
       <a href="/wiki/Magna_Graecia" title="Magna Graecia">
        Greek
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_peoples_of_Italy" title="Ancient peoples of Italy">
        Italic
       </a>
       population there.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011285_16-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011285-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fabian_strategy">
        Fabian strategy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Fabian strategy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Fabian_strategy" title="Fabian strategy">
        Fabian strategy
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Altar_Domitius_Ahenobarbus_Louvre_n2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1150" data-file-width="3150" height="73" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Altar_Domitius_Ahenobarbus_Louvre_n2.jpg/200px-Altar_Domitius_Ahenobarbus_Louvre_n2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Altar_Domitius_Ahenobarbus_Louvre_n2.jpg/300px-Altar_Domitius_Ahenobarbus_Louvre_n2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Altar_Domitius_Ahenobarbus_Louvre_n2.jpg/400px-Altar_Domitius_Ahenobarbus_Louvre_n2.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Altar_Domitius_Ahenobarbus_Louvre_n2.jpg" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         Detail of frieze showing the equipment of a soldier in the
         <a href="/wiki/Maniple_(military_unit)" title="Maniple (military unit)">
          manipular
         </a>
         Roman legion (left). Note mail armour, oval shield and helmet with plume (probably horsehair). The soldier in the centre is an officer (bronze cuirass, mantle), prob. a
         <i>
          tribunus militum
         </i>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
          <a href="#cite_note-18">
           [18]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <a href="/wiki/Altar_of_Domitius_Ahenobarbus" title="Altar of Domitius Ahenobarbus">
          From an altar
         </a>
         built by
         <a href="/wiki/Gnaeus_Domitius_Ahenobarbus_(consul_122_BC)" title="Gnaeus Domitius Ahenobarbus (consul 122 BC)">
          Gnaeus Domitius Ahenobarbus
         </a>
         , consul in 122 BC.
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_du_Louvre" title="Musée du Louvre">
          Musée du Louvre
         </a>
         , Paris
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sg0542.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="224" data-file-width="450" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Sg0542.jpg/200px-Sg0542.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Sg0542.jpg/300px-Sg0542.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Sg0542.jpg/400px-Sg0542.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sg0542.jpg" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         Roman coin issued during the Second Punic war showing (obverse) the god of war
         <a href="/wiki/Mars_(mythology)" title="Mars (mythology)">
          Mars
         </a>
         and (reverse) a very rare image of a Roman cavalryman of the time. Note the plumed helmet, long spear (
         <i>
          hasta
         </i>
         ), small round shield, flowing mantle. Roman cavalry was levied from the
         <i>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Equestrian_order" title="Equestrian order">
           equites
          </a>
         </i>
         , or noble knights, until c. 338 BC and thereafter also from the First Class of commoners under the
         <a href="/wiki/Centuria" title="Centuria">
          centuriate
         </a>
         organisation. Bronze
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Quincunx_(Roman_coin)" title="Quincunx (Roman coin)">
           quincunx
          </a>
         </i>
         from
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Larinum" title="Larinum">
          Larinum
         </a>
         mint
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The defeat at Lake Trasimene put the Romans in an immense state of panic, fearing for the very existence of their city. The Senate decided to resort to the traditional emergency measure of appointing a
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Roman_dictator" title="Roman dictator">
         dictator
        </a>
       </i>
       , a temporary commander-in-chief who would unite military authority, which was normally divided between the two consuls, for six months. The usual procedure required the presence of a consul to appoint the
       <i>
        dictator
       </i>
       . Since one consul (Flaminius) was dead and the other (Servilius) away with the only army left in Italy, the Senate resolved to elect a dictator itself. As this was unconstitutional, the person appointed,
       <a href="/wiki/Quintus_Fabius_Maximus_Verrucosus" title="Quintus Fabius Maximus Verrucosus">
        Quintus Fabius Maximus
       </a>
       , was given the title of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Roman_dictator#Replacement_of_the_dictatorate" title="Roman dictator">
         prodictator
        </a>
       </i>
       (acting dictator) although he held the same powers as a dictator. The Senate also appointed his
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Magister_equitum" title="Magister equitum">
         magister equitum
        </a>
       </i>
       ("master of cavalry", who acted as his second-in-command) instead of allowing the dictator to choose one himself as was the normal rule:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marcus_Minucius_Rufus_(consul_221_BC)" title="Marcus Minucius Rufus (consul 221 BC)">
        M. Minucius Rufus
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livy_3-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-Livy-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/10907/10907-h/10907-h.htm#d8" rel="nofollow">
          22.8
         </a>
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Departing from the Roman military tradition of engaging the enemy in pitched battle as soon as possible, Fabius invented the
       <a href="/wiki/Fabian_strategy" title="Fabian strategy">
        Fabian strategy
       </a>
       : refusing open battle with his opponent, but constantly skirmishing with small detachments of the enemy. This course was not popular among the soldiers, earning Fabius the nickname Cunctator ("delayer"), since he seemed to avoid battle while Italy was being ravaged by the enemy. Moreover, it was widely feared that, if Hannibal continued to plunder Italy unopposed, the terrified allies, believing that Rome was incapable of protecting them, might defect and pledge their allegiance to the Carthaginians. As a countermeasure, residents of villages were encouraged to post lookouts, so that they could gather their livestock and possessions in time and take refuge in fortified towns that the enemy could not yet take. Fabius' policy was to shadow Hannibal by moving on the heights parallel to the Carthaginian movements on the plains, to avoid Hannibal's cavalry which was supreme on flat terrain. This demanded great care, since the Carthaginian tried with all his skill to ambush the Romans. For this reason, a new marching formation, with three parallel columns of infantry, was developed instead of the single column that had been in use at Lake Trasimene.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011285_16-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011285-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Fabius' constant harassment of Hannibal's force handicapped the latter's command abilities and gained many prisoners. Both commanders decided that they would exchange prisoners under the same conditions as in the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Punic_War" title="First Punic War">
        First Punic War
       </a>
       . Although the Carthaginians returned to the Romans several hundred more prisoners than they received and were thus expecting monetary compensation, the Senate was reluctant to pay. However, the estates of Fabius had not been touched by the Carthaginian pillage parties in order to incite distrust against him. Fabius now sold these estates to pay the enemy army for the received surplus of prisoners.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011285_16-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011285-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Having ravaged
       <a href="/wiki/Apulia" title="Apulia">
        Apulia
       </a>
       without provoking Fabius into a battle, Hannibal decided to march through
       <a href="/wiki/Samnium" title="Samnium">
        Samnium
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Campania" title="Campania">
        Campania
       </a>
       , one of the richest and most fertile provinces of Italy, hoping that the devastation would draw Fabius into battle. The latter was aware that there were excellent opportunities to trap the Carthaginian force on the Campanian plain and to force Hannibal to fight in the surrounding mountains on ground of his own choice. As the year wore on, Hannibal decided that it would be unwise to winter in the already devastated plains of Campania but Fabius had ensured that all the mountain passes offering an exit were blocked. This situation led to the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ager_Falernus" title="Battle of Ager Falernus">
        night battle of Ager Falernus
       </a>
       in which the Carthaginians made good their escape by tricking the Romans into believing that they were heading to the heights above them. The Romans were thus decoyed and the Carthaginians slipped through the undefended pass with all their baggage train. This was a severe blow to Fabius’ prestige.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011285_16-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011285-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Minucius, the
       <i>
        magister equitum
       </i>
       , was one of the leading voices in the army against the adoption of the Fabian Strategy. As soon as he scored a minor success, by winning a skirmish with the Carthaginians, the Senate promoted Minucius to the same
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Imperium" title="Imperium">
         imperium
        </a>
       </i>
       (power of command) as Fabius, whom he accused of cowardice. In consequence, the two men decided to split the army between them. Minucius' division was swiftly lured into an ambush by Hannibal in the flat country of
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Geronium" title="Battle of Geronium">
        Geronium
       </a>
       . Fabius rushed to his co-commander's assistance and Hannibal's forces immediately retreated. Subsequently, Minucius accepted Fabius' authority and ended their political conflict.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011285_16-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011285-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Seeking_a_decisive_engagement">
        Seeking a decisive engagement
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Seeking a decisive engagement">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cannae" title="Battle of Cannae">
        Battle of Cannae
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Fabius became unpopular in Rome, since his tactics did not lead to a quick end to the war. The Roman populace derided the
       <i>
        Cunctator
       </i>
       , and at the elections of 216 BC elected as consuls
       <a href="/wiki/Gaius_Terentius_Varro" title="Gaius Terentius Varro">
        Gaius Terentius Varro
       </a>
       who advocated pursuing a more aggressive war strategy and
       <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Aemilius_Paullus_(consul_219_BC)" title="Lucius Aemilius Paullus (consul 219 BC)">
        Lucius Aemilius Paullus
       </a>
       , who advocated a strategy in the middle between the Fabian tactics and the tactics suggested by Varro.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011286_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011286-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the campaign of 217 BC, Hannibal had failed to obtain a following among the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Italic_peoples" title="Ancient Italic peoples">
        Italics
       </a>
       . In the spring of 216 BC, he took the initiative and seized the large supply depot at
       <a href="/wiki/Cannae" title="Cannae">
        Cannae
       </a>
       in the Apulian plain. Thus, by seizing Cannae, Hannibal had placed himself between the Romans and their crucial source of supply. The Roman Senate authorised the raising of double-sized armies by the consuls Varro and Aemilius Paullus, a force of 86,000 men, the largest in Roman history up to that point.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011286_19-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011286-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Cannae,_215_BC_-_Initial_Roman_attack.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="571" data-file-width="742" height="308" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Battle_of_Cannae%2C_215_BC_-_Initial_Roman_attack.png/400px-Battle_of_Cannae%2C_215_BC_-_Initial_Roman_attack.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Battle_of_Cannae%2C_215_BC_-_Initial_Roman_attack.png/600px-Battle_of_Cannae%2C_215_BC_-_Initial_Roman_attack.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fb/Battle_of_Cannae%2C_215_BC_-_Initial_Roman_attack.png 2x" width="400"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Cannae,_215_BC_-_Initial_Roman_attack.png" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         Opening and decisive phase of the
         <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cannae" title="Battle of Cannae">
          Battle of Cannae
         </a>
         , 216 BC. The Carthaginian cavalry (made up of Gauls and Iberians) routed the much weaker Roman cavalry on the Roman right wing, then raced round the rear of the Roman line to attack from behind the Romans' allied Latin cavalry on the Roman left, who were already engaged with Hannibal's Numidian horse. The Latin cavalry was then destroyed. The victorious Carthaginian cavalry was then free to attack the Roman infantry line from the rear. The battle confirmed the superiority of Hannibal's cavalry, in both numbers and training, over the Roman and Latin citizen levies. From this time, the Romans relied heavily on non-Italian allied cavalry and, around the start of the 1st century BC, legionary cavalry was abolished altogether
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The consuls Aemilius Paullus and Varro resolved to confront Hannibal and marched southward to
       <a href="/wiki/Apulia" title="Apulia">
        Apulia
       </a>
       . After a two-day march, they found him on the left bank of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aufidus_River" title="Aufidus River">
        Aufidus River
       </a>
       , and encamped 10 km (6.2 mi) away. Hannibal capitalized on Varro's eagerness and drew him into a trap by using an
       <a href="/wiki/Envelopment" title="Envelopment">
        envelopment
       </a>
       tactic that eliminated the Roman numerical advantage by shrinking the surface area where combat could occur. Hannibal drew up his least reliable infantry in the centre of a semicircle, with the wings composed of the Gallic and Numidian horse. The Roman legions forced their way through Hannibal's weak centre, but the Libyan Mercenaries on the wings swung around their advance, menacing their flanks.
