The onslaught of Hannibal's cavalry was irresistible, and the cavalry commander
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hasdrubal,_commander_of_the_service_corps" title="Hasdrubal, commander of the service corps">
        Hasdrubal
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livy_3-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-Livy-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/10907/10907-h/10907-h.htm#d46" rel="nofollow">
          22.45
         </a>
        </span>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (not to be confused with Hannibal's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hasdrubal_(Barcid)" title="Hasdrubal (Barcid)">
        brother
       </a>
       who was campaigning in Iberia
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livy_3-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-Livy-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/10907/10907-h/10907-h.htm#e26" rel="nofollow">
          23.26
         </a>
        </span>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ), routed the Roman cavalry on the Roman right wing and then swept around the rear of the Roman line and attacked Varro's cavalry on the Roman left, and then the legions, from behind. As a result, the Roman army was surrounded with no means of escape. Due to these brilliant tactics, Hannibal, with much inferior numbers, managed to destroy all but a small remnant of this force. Depending on the source, it is estimated that 50,000–70,000 Romans were killed or captured at Cannae.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Livy" title="Livy">
        Livy
       </a>
       notes, "How much more serious was the defeat of Cannae, than those which preceded it can be seen by the behaviour of Rome’s allies; before that fateful day, their loyalty remained unshaken, now it began to waver for the simple reason that they despaired of Roman power."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livy_3-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-Livy-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/10907/10907-h/10907-h.htm#d61" rel="nofollow">
          22.61
         </a>
        </span>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During that same year, the Greek cities in Sicily were induced to revolt against Roman political control, while the Macedonian king,
       <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Macedon" title="Philip V of Macedon">
        Philip V
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Macedonian%E2%80%93Carthaginian_Treaty" title="Macedonian–Carthaginian Treaty">
        pledged his support
       </a>
       to Hannibal – thus initiating the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Macedonian_War" title="First Macedonian War">
        First Macedonian War
       </a>
       against Rome. Hannibal also secured an alliance with newly appointed King
       <a href="/wiki/Hieronymus_of_Syracuse" title="Hieronymus of Syracuse">
        Hieronymus of Syracuse
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Taranto" title="Taranto">
        Tarentum
       </a>
       also came over to him around that time. Hannibal refused to attack Rome after Cannae. The Romans looked back on Hannibal's indecision as what saved Rome from certain defeat. Hannibal merely sent a delegation to Rome to negotiate a peace and another one offering to release his Roman prisoners of war for ransom, but Rome rejected all offers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011249_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011249-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Establishing_a_Carthaginian_alliance_in_Italy">
        Establishing a Carthaginian alliance in Italy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Establishing a Carthaginian alliance in Italy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         For a detailed analysis of Hannibal's relations with Roman allies, see:
         <a href="/wiki/Socii#2nd_Punic_War" title="Socii">
          Socii
         </a>
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Second_Punic_war.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="869" data-file-width="1583" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Second_Punic_war.png/220px-Second_Punic_war.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Second_Punic_war.png/330px-Second_Punic_war.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Second_Punic_war.png/440px-Second_Punic_war.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Second_Punic_war.png" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         Hannibal's allies in Italy.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Via_Appia_map.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="692" data-file-width="1280" height="108" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Via_Appia_map.jpg/200px-Via_Appia_map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Via_Appia_map.jpg/300px-Via_Appia_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Via_Appia_map.jpg/400px-Via_Appia_map.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Via_Appia_map.jpg" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         Trace of the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Via_Appia" title="Via Appia">
          Via Appia
         </a>
         imposed on a satellite picture of southern Italy, showing the location of many of the Greek cities fought over by Hannibal and the Romans. The original Via Appia is in white. The alternative road (in pink) was constructed 400 years later under emperor
         <a href="/wiki/Trajan" title="Trajan">
          Trajan
         </a>
         (ruled 98-117). But the route was already a busy one in Hannibal's time and repeatedly used by him
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After Cannae, several south Italian cities allied themselves to Hannibal: the
       <a href="/wiki/Apulia" title="Apulia">
        Apulian
       </a>
       towns of
       <a href="/wiki/Salapia" title="Salapia">
        Salapia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Arpi" title="Arpi">
        Arpi
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ordona" title="Ordona">
        Herdonia
       </a>
       and many of the
       <a href="/wiki/Lucania" title="Lucania">
        Lucanians
       </a>
       . Mago marched south with a Carthaginian army detachment and, some weeks later, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bruttian" title="Bruttian">
        Bruttians
       </a>
       joined him. Simultaneously, Hannibal marched north with part of his forces and was joined by the
       <a href="/wiki/Hirpini" title="Hirpini">
        Hirpini
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Caudini" title="Caudini">
        Caudini
       </a>
       , two of the three
       <a href="/wiki/Samnium" title="Samnium">
        Samnite
       </a>
       cantons. The greatest gain was the second largest city of Italy,
       <a href="/wiki/Capua" title="Capua">
        Capua
       </a>
       , when Hannibal's army marched into
       <a href="/wiki/Campania" title="Campania">
        Campania
       </a>
       in 216 BC. The inhabitants of Capua held limited Roman citizenship and the aristocracy was linked to the Romans via marriage and friendship, but the possibility of becoming the supreme city of Italy after the evident Roman disasters proved too strong a temptation. The treaty between them and Hannibal can be described as an agreement of friendship, since the Capuans had no obligations, but provided the harbour through which Hannibal was reinforced.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       By 215 BC, Hannibal's alliance system covered the bulk of southern Italy, save for the
       <a href="/wiki/Magna_Graecia" title="Magna Graecia">
        Greek cities
       </a>
       along the coast (except
       <a href="/wiki/Crotone" title="Crotone">
        Croton
       </a>
       , which was conquered by his allies),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhegium" title="Rhegium">
        Rhegium
       </a>
       , and the Latin colonies of
       <a href="/wiki/Benevento" title="Benevento">
        Beneventum
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lucera" title="Lucera">
        Luceria
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Samnium" title="Samnium">
        Samnium
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venusia" title="Venusia">
        Venusia
       </a>
       in Apulia,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brundisium" title="Brundisium">
        Brundisium
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Paestum" title="Paestum">
        Paestum
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011313_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011313-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The independent Gaul he had established in northern Italy was still out of Roman control.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The port city of
       <a href="/wiki/Locri" title="Locri">
        Locri
       </a>
       defected to Carthage in the summer of 215 and was immediately used to build up the Carthaginian forces in Italy. A Carthaginian fleet landed in Locri and 4,000 Numidian cavalry, 40 war elephants, money, grain and other provisions, all under the command of Bomilcar joined Hanno's army in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bruttium" title="Bruttium">
        Bruttium
       </a>
       . It was the only time during the war that Carthage succeeded in sending reinforcements to Hannibal in Italy. A second force under Mago in 215, consisting of 12,000 infantry, 1,500 cavalry and 20 elephants guarded by 60 warships, was also meant to land in Italy but bolstered Hasdrubal in Spain instead after the Carthaginian defeat there at Dertosa.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos201175_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos201175-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Hannibal had been able to win over a major allied base by his tremendous military success. He also regarded it as essential to take the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Nola" title="Nola">
        Nola
       </a>
       , a Roman fortress in Campania, a region that linked his various allies geographically and contained his most important harbour for supply. Prior to his first attempt, the pro-Carthage faction in the city had been eliminated by the Romans, so there was no chance of the city being betrayed. Hannibal repeatedly tried to take this city by assault or siege, but was thwarted three times, in
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nola_(216_BC)" title="Battle of Nola (216 BC)">
        216
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nola_(215_BC)" title="Battle of Nola (215 BC)">
        215
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nola_(214_BC)" title="Battle of Nola (214 BC)">
        214
       </a>
       , by forces led by
       <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Claudius_Marcellus" title="Marcus Claudius Marcellus">
        Marcus Claudius Marcellus
       </a>
       . In 215 Hannibal besieged and starved
       <a href="/wiki/Casilinum" title="Casilinum">
        Casilinum
       </a>
       into submission, the other important site for controlling Campania.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011301_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011301-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syracuse,_Italy" title="Syracuse, Italy">
        Syracuse
       </a>
       , located on the sea routes Hannibal needed to secure supply, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lilybaeum" title="Lilybaeum">
        Lilybaeum
       </a>
       both remained in Roman hands. Hannibal was aided by the fact that
       <a href="/wiki/Hiero_II_of_Syracuse" title="Hiero II of Syracuse">
        Hiero II
       </a>
       , the old tyrant of Syracuse and a staunch Roman ally, had died and his successor
       <a href="/wiki/Hieronymus_of_Syracuse" title="Hieronymus of Syracuse">
        Hieronymus
       </a>
       was discontented with his position in the Roman alliance. Hannibal dispatched two of his lieutenants, who were of Syracusian origin to negotiate with
       <a href="/wiki/Hieronymus_of_Syracuse" title="Hieronymus of Syracuse">
        Hieronymus
       </a>
       . They succeeded in winning Syracuse over, at the price, however, of making the whole of Sicily a Syracusan possession. The Syracusans' ambitions were great, but the army they fielded was no match for the arriving Roman force, leading to the
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Syracuse_(214%E2%80%93212_BC)" title="Siege of Syracuse (214–212 BC)">
        Siege of Syracuse
       </a>
       from 214 BC onwards.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011327_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011327-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The essence of Hannibal's campaign in Italy was to fight the Romans by using local resources and raising recruits from among the local population. His subordinate Hanno was able to raise troops in
       <a href="/wiki/Samnium" title="Samnium">
        Samnium
       </a>
       , but the Romans intercepted these new levies in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Beneventum_(214_BC)" title="Battle of Beneventum (214 BC)">
        Battle of Beneventum (214 BC)
       </a>
       and eliminated them before they came under the feared leadership of Hannibal. Hannibal could win allies, but defending them against the Romans was a new and difficult problem, as the Romans could still field multiple armies greatly outnumbering his own forces. Thus Fabius was able to take the Carthaginian ally
       <a href="/wiki/Arpi" title="Arpi">
        Arpi
       </a>
       in 213 BC.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011312_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011312-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Eastern_Mediterranean_and_Ionian_Sea_.28218.E2.80.93213_BC.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Mediterranean_and_Ionian_Sea_(218–213_BC)">
        Eastern Mediterranean and Ionian Sea (218–213 BC)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Eastern Mediterranean and Ionian Sea (218–213 BC)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/First_Macedonian_War" title="First Macedonian War">
        First Macedonian War
       </a>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        217 BC – letter from Hannibal after
        <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lake_Trasimene" title="Battle of Lake Trasimene">
         Battle of Lake Trasimene
        </a>
        leading to war preparations
       </li>
       <li>
        217–216 BC –
        <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Macedon" title="Philip V of Macedon">
         Philip V of Macedon
        </a>
        builds a fleet of 100
        <a href="/wiki/Lembus" title="Lembus">
         lembi
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        216 BC – ambassadors to Hannibal after
        <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cannae" title="Battle of Cannae">
         Battle of Cannae
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        214 BC –
        <a href="/wiki/First_Macedonian_War" title="First Macedonian War">
         First Macedonian War
        </a>
        officially starts
       </li>
       <li>
        214 BC – naval expeditions from Macedonia
       </li>
       <li>
        213 BC – land expedition to Lissus
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span id="The_tide_turns_.28212.E2.80.93207_BC.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_tide_turns_(212–207_BC)">
        The tide turns (212–207 BC)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: The tide turns (212–207 BC)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span id="Western_Mediterranean_.28212.E2.80.93207_BC.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Western_Mediterranean_(212–207_BC)">
        Western Mediterranean (212–207 BC)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Western Mediterranean (212–207 BC)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Defeat_of_the_first_expedition">
        Defeat of the first expedition
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Defeat of the first expedition">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dc-hannibal-coin.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="450" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Dc-hannibal-coin.png/220px-Dc-hannibal-coin.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Dc-hannibal-coin.png/330px-Dc-hannibal-coin.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Dc-hannibal-coin.png/440px-Dc-hannibal-coin.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dc-hannibal-coin.png" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a href="/wiki/Carthaginian_currency" title="Carthaginian currency">
          Carthaginian coin
         </a>
         possibly depicting
         <a href="/wiki/Hannibal" title="Hannibal">
          Hannibal
         </a>
         as
         <a href="/wiki/Hercules" title="Hercules">
          Hercules
         </a>
         (i.e.
         <a href="/wiki/Heracles" title="Heracles">
          Heracles
         </a>
         )
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In Iberia, the Scipio brothers hired 20,000 Celtiberian mercenaries to reinforce their army of 30,000 infantry and 3,000 cavalry. Observing that the Carthaginian armies were deployed separately from each other, with Hasdrubal Barca and 15,000 troops near Amtorgis, and Mago Barca and Hasdrubal Gisco, both with 10,000 troops, further to the west of Hasdrubal, the Scipio brothers planned to split their forces.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Publius_Scipio" title="Publius Scipio">
        Publius Scipio
       </a>
       moved 20,000 Roman and allied soldiers to attack Mago Barca near
       <a href="/wiki/Castulo" title="Castulo">
        Castulo
       </a>
       , while
       <a href="/wiki/Gnaeus_Cornelius_Scipio_Calvus" title="Gnaeus Cornelius Scipio Calvus">
        Gnaeus Scipio
       </a>
       took one double legion (10,000 troops) and the mercenaries to attack Hasdrubal Barca. This stratagem resulted in 2 battles, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Castulo" title="Battle of Castulo">
        Battle of Castulo
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ilorca" title="Battle of Ilorca">
        Battle of Ilorca
       </a>
       , which occurred within a few days of each other, usually combined as the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Upper_Baetis" title="Battle of the Upper Baetis">
        Battle of the Upper Baetis
       </a>
       (211 BC). Both battles ended in clear defeats for the Romans as Hasdrubal had bribed the Roman mercenaries to desert and return home without a fight.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011322_10-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011322-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As a result of the battle, the Romans were forced to retreat to their stronghold of Northern Iberia, from which the Carthaginians could not expel them. It is notable that the Roman soldiers decided to elect a new leader, since both commanders had been killed, a practice hitherto known only in Carthaginian or Hellenistic armies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011322_10-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011322-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Roman_expedition_to_Iberia">
        Second Roman expedition to Iberia
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Second Roman expedition to Iberia">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       In 210 BC, Scipio Africanus arrived in Iberia on with a proconsular
       <i>
        imperium
       </i>
       and more reinforcements that increased the strength of his army to 28,000 infantry and 3,000 cavalry.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011323_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011323-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In a brilliant assault in 209 BC, Scipio succeeded in capturing
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cartagena_(209_BC)" title="Battle of Cartagena (209 BC)">
        Cartago Nova
       </a>
       , which was the centre of Carthaginian power in Iberia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011323_33-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011323-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He defeated Hasdrubal in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Baecula" title="Battle of Baecula">
        Battle of Baecula
       </a>
       (208 BC), but was not able to prevent him from continuing his march to Italy in order to reinforce his brother Hannibal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011323_33-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011323-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ilipa" title="Battle of Ilipa">
        Battle of Ilipa
       </a>
       (206 BC), Scipio defeated a combined army under the command of
       <a href="/wiki/Mago_Barca" title="Mago Barca">
        Mago Barca
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hasdrubal_Gisco" title="Hasdrubal Gisco">
        Hasdrubal Gisco
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Masinissa" title="Masinissa">
        Masinissa
       </a>
       , thus bringing Carthaginian dominance in Iberia to an end.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011323_33-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011323-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Carthage still succeeded in recruiting thousands of mercenaries from Iberia after 206 BC despite Rome's nominal control.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011333_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011333-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Central_Mediterranean_.28212.E2.80.93207_BC.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Central_Mediterranean_(212–207_BC)">
        Central Mediterranean (212–207 BC)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Central Mediterranean (212–207 BC)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span id="The_war_in_Sicily_214.E2.80.93210_BC">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_war_in_Sicily_214–210_BC">
        The war in Sicily 214–210 BC
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: The war in Sicily 214–210 BC">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Archimedes_and_Hiero_of_Syracuse.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="645" height="273" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Archimedes_and_Hiero_of_Syracuse.jpg/220px-Archimedes_and_Hiero_of_Syracuse.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Archimedes_and_Hiero_of_Syracuse.jpg/330px-Archimedes_and_Hiero_of_Syracuse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Archimedes_and_Hiero_of_Syracuse.jpg/440px-Archimedes_and_Hiero_of_Syracuse.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Archimedes_and_Hiero_of_Syracuse.jpg" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         Hiero of Syracuse calls Archimedes to fortify the city.
         <a href="/wiki/Sebastiano_Ricci" title="Sebastiano Ricci">
          Sebastiano Ricci
         </a>
         , 1720.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Syracuse_(214%E2%80%93212_BC)" title="Siege of Syracuse (214–212 BC)">
        Siege of Syracuse
       </a>
       , from 214 BC onwards, was marked by
       <a href="/wiki/Archimedes" title="Archimedes">
        Archimedes
       </a>
       ' ingenuity in inventing war machines that made it impossible for the Romans to make any gains with traditional methods of siege warfare.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011328_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011328-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A Carthaginian army of 25,000 infantry, 3,000 cavalry and 12 elephants under Himilco was sent to relieve the city in 213, landing at and capturing
       <a href="/wiki/Heraclea_Minoa" title="Heraclea Minoa">
        Heraclea Minoa
       </a>
       and followed up by taking
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agrigentum" title="Agrigentum">
        Agrigentum
       </a>
       . Himilco linked up with the remaining 500 cavalry of Hippocrates' once 10,000-strong Syracusan army that had attempted to join with the Carthaginians but had been defeated by Marcellus' Romans. Himilco faced up against Marcellus outside Syracuse but the Romans preferred to wait for reinforcements in the form of one legion and allied contingents and Himilco not only failed to force a battle against the outnumbered Romans but poor intelligence sent him the wrong way while attempting to intercept the Roman reinforcements. At the same time, a Carthaginian fleet under Bomilcar sailed into Syracuse's great harbor with 55 warships.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011329_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011329-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After Himilco's failure to defeat Marcellus, Bomilcar sailed away with his fleet while Himilco began taking over Roman-garrisoned towns in Sicily. The Roman garrison at
       <a href="/wiki/Morgantina" title="Morgantina">
        Morgantina
       </a>
       was betrayed from within and Himilco took over large stores of grain and other supplies. The Roman garrison commander at nearby
       <a href="/wiki/Enna" title="Enna">
        Enna
       </a>
       heard of Morgantina's treachery and massacred Enna's civilian population. A general revolt against Roman rule in Sicily erupted, with Roman garrisons either being expelled from towns or exterminated by the rebels with Carthaginian support. Once again, Himilco did not attack Marcellus despite the help from Sicilian rebels and went to winter quarters at Agrigentum instead.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011329_36-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011329-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the spring of 212, Marcellus stormed the walls of Syracuse in a surprise night assault and conquered several districts inside the city. Himilco and Bomilcar now made real efforts to lift the siege, Himilco marching his army up to the Roman camp and Bomilcar arriving with 90 quinqueremes, of which he gave 55 to
       <a href="/wiki/Epicydes" title="Epicydes">
        Epicydes
       </a>
       , sailing away and re-appearing several days later with 100 more warships. Himilco's army was crippled by the
       <a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">
        plague
       </a>
       and when the Syracusans inside the city and Hippocrates' troops outside the city attacked the Romans, all of their attempts were beaten back. Himilco and Hippocrates died soon thereafter of the disease. While the Romans also suffered, Marcellus saved most of his men by bringing them all inside the city. Bomilcar exited Syracuse's harbor without being troubled by the Romans and re-appeared with 130 quinqueremes and 700 supply ships to lift the siege for good. Poor weather prevented him from arriving before being intercepted by 100 ships under Marcellus. Before battle could be joined, Bomilcar decided to flee, ordering the supply ships to return home while the Carthaginian battlefleet sailed to Tarentum. Syracuse fell soon after and Archimedes was killed by a Roman soldier.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011329_36-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011329-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 211 BC Hannibal sent to Sicily a force of Numidian cavalry led by the skilled Liby-Phoenician officer Mottones, who inflicted heavy losses on Marcellus' army through hit-and-run attacks. Agrigentum's Carthaginian garrison commander Hanno grew jealous of Mottones' success and when the latter was away dealing with some mutinous Numidians, Hanno with the main Carthaginian army decided to attack Marcellus without waiting for Mottones. The Numidians with Hanno refused to fight without their commander and Hanno's outnumbered force was promptly crushed by Marcellus at the
       <a href="/wiki/Himera" title="Himera">
        Himera
       </a>
       river.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011330_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011330-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Carthage sent more reinforcements to Sicily, including 8,000 infantry and 3,000 Numidian cavalry. Hanno and Muttines went over to the offensive, capturing
       <a href="/wiki/Macella" title="Macella">
        Macella
       </a>
       and re-capturing Morgantina. Marcellus was succeeded by the praetor Marcus Cornelius who first dealt with indiscipline in the Roman army, after which he checked the Carthaginian progress by taking Morgantina. The hyper-aggressive Roman consul
       <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Valerius_Laevinus" title="Marcus Valerius Laevinus">
        Marcus Valerius Laevinus
       </a>
       took charge in 210 BC and immediately marched on Agrigentum to evict Carthage from Sicily. Hanno demoted Mottones and Hanno's son was given the command of the cavalry instead. Mottones betrayed the Carthaginian cause and opened the gates of Agrigentum to the Romans. The Romans massacred the population of the city or sold them to slavery. Hanno and Epicydes fled to Carthage in a merchant ship. Laevinus captured 66 other Sicilian towns, of which 40 surrendered and 26 were taken through force or treachery.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011330_37-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011330-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He put Sicilian farms back into production and the supply of grain to Rome was resumed in 209 BC.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011311_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011311-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="Climax_and_fall_of_Hannibal.27s_alliance">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climax_and_fall_of_Hannibal's_alliance">
        Climax and fall of Hannibal's alliance
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Climax and fall of Hannibal's alliance">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tarentum_Hannibal.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="246" data-file-width="500" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Tarentum_Hannibal.jpg/200px-Tarentum_Hannibal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Tarentum_Hannibal.jpg/300px-Tarentum_Hannibal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Tarentum_Hannibal.jpg/400px-Tarentum_Hannibal.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tarentum_Hannibal.jpg" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         Coin issued by the city of
         <a href="/wiki/Taranto" title="Taranto">
          Tarentum
         </a>
         during the period of Hannibal's control c. 212–208 BC showing (obverse) youth on horseback and (reverse) boy riding dolphin, the traditional symbol of Tarentine coins. Note the legend ΤΑΡΑΣ (TARAS) the Greek name for the city. Silver
         <i>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Didrachm" title="Didrachm">
           didrachm
          </a>
         </i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tomba_archimede.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Tomba_archimede.JPG/200px-Tomba_archimede.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Tomba_archimede.JPG/300px-Tomba_archimede.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Tomba_archimede.JPG/400px-Tomba_archimede.JPG 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tomba_archimede.JPG" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         Ancient Greek tomb at
         <a href="/wiki/Syracuse,_Sicily" title="Syracuse, Sicily">
          Syracuse
         </a>
         , Sicily, believed to be that of
         <a href="/wiki/Archimedes" title="Archimedes">
          Archimedes
         </a>
         (with decorative lintel)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The climax of Carthaginian expansion was reached when the largest Greek city in Italy,
       <a href="/wiki/Taranto" title="Taranto">
        Tarentum
       </a>
       , switched sides in 212 BC. The
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tarentum_(212_BC)" title="Battle of Tarentum (212 BC)">
        Battle of Tarentum (212 BC)
       </a>
       was a carefully planned coup by Hannibal and members of the city's democratic faction. There were two separate successful assaults on the gates of the city. This enabled the Carthaginian army, which had approached unobserved behind a screen of marauding Numidian horsemen, to enter the city by surprise and take all but the citadel where the Romans and their supporting faction were able to rally. The Carthaginians failed to take the citadel, but subsequent fortifications around this Roman stronghold put the city under Carthaginian control. However, the harbour was blocked and warships had to be transported overland to be launched at sea.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Capua_(212_BC)" title="Battle of Capua (212 BC)">
        Battle of Capua (212 BC)
       </a>
       was a stalemate. The Romans decided to end the siege of Capua. As a result, the Capuan cavalry was reinforced with half of the available Numidian cavalry of 2,000.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Beneventum_(212_BC)" title="Battle of Beneventum (212 BC)">
        Battle of Beneventum (212 BC)
       </a>
       , Hanno the Elder was again defeated, this time by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quintus_Fulvius_Flaccus" title="Quintus Fulvius Flaccus">
        Quintus Fulvius Flaccus
       </a>
       , who also captured his camp.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011316_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011316-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the following
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Silarus" title="Battle of the Silarus">
        Battle of the Silarus
       </a>
       , in the same year, the Romans under Marcus Centenius were ambushed and lost all but 1,000 of their 16,000 effectives.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011301_30-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011301-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Also, in 212 BC, the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Herdonia_(212_BC)" title="Battle of Herdonia (212 BC)">
        Battle of Herdonia
       </a>
       resulted in another Roman defeat, with only 2,000 Romans out of a force of 18,000 surviving a direct attack by Hannibal's numerically superior forces, combined with an ambush that cut off the Roman line of retreat.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos201185_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos201185-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011253_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011253-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       This phase of the war was marked by the fall of major and minor cities to the Romans, although Hannibal was still able to prevail on the battlefield and thus lift some sieges.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Servian_Wall.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Servian_Wall.JPG/200px-Servian_Wall.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Servian_Wall.JPG/300px-Servian_Wall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Servian_Wall.JPG/400px-Servian_Wall.JPG 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Servian_Wall.JPG" title="Suurenna">
          </a>
         </div>
         A section of Rome's
         <a href="/wiki/Servian_Wall" title="Servian Wall">
          Servian Wall
         </a>
         at
         <a href="/wiki/Roma_Termini_railway_station" title="Roma Termini railway station">
          Termini
         </a>
         railway station. It was this wall that dissuaded Hannibal from attempting a direct attack on Rome.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In a second
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Capua_(211_BC)" title="Battle of Capua (211 BC)">
        Battle of Capua (211 BC)
       </a>
       , Hannibal again tried to regain use of his main harbour as in the previous year, by luring the Romans into a pitched battle. He was unsuccessful, and was also unable to lift the siege by assaulting the besiegers' defences. So he tried a strategem of staging a march towards Rome, hoping in this way to compel the enemy to abandon the siege and rush to defend their home city. However, only part of the besieging force left for Rome and, under continued siege, Capua fell to Rome soon afterwards. Near Rome he fought another pitched battle.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011300_42-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011300-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The second
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Herdonia_(210_BC)" title="Battle of Herdonia (210 BC)">
        Battle of Herdonia (210 BC)
       </a>
       was fought to lift the Roman siege of that allied city. Hannibal caught the proconsul
       <a href="/wiki/Gnaeus_Fulvius_Centumalus_Maximus" title="Gnaeus Fulvius Centumalus Maximus">
        Gnaeus Fulvius Centumalus
       </a>
       off guard during his siege of Herdonia and destroyed his army in a pitched battle with up to 13,000 Romans dead of 20,000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011300_42-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011300-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The defection of the allied city of Salapia in Apulia in 210 BC was achieved by treachery: the inhabitants massacred the Numidian garrison and went over to the Romans.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011350_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011350-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 210 BC, the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Numistro" title="Battle of Numistro">
        Battle of Numistro
       </a>
       between Marcellus and Hannibal was inconclusive, but the Romans stayed on his heels until the also inconclusive
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Canusium" title="Battle of Canusium">
        Battle of Canusium
       </a>
       in 209 BC.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011301–302_44-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011301–302-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the meantime, this battle enabled another Roman army under Fabius to approach Tarentum and take it by treachery in the second
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tarentum_(209_BC)" title="Battle of Tarentum (209 BC)">
        Battle of Tarentum (209 BC)
       </a>
       . Hannibal, at that time, had been able to disengage from Marcellus and was only 8.0 km (5 mi) away when the city, under the command of Carthalo, who was bound to Fabius by an agreement of hospitality, fell.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011372_45-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011372-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="Hasdrubal.27s_failed_reinforcement">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hasdrubal's_failed_reinforcement">
        Hasdrubal's failed reinforcement
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Punic_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Hasdrubal's failed reinforcement">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grumentum" title="Battle of Grumentum">
        Battle of Grumentum
       </a>
       was an inconclusive fight in 207 BC between
       <a href="/wiki/Gaius_Claudius_Nero" title="Gaius Claudius Nero">
        Gaius Claudius Nero
       </a>
       and Hannibal. In the aftermath of the battle, Nero was able to trick Hannibal into believing that the whole Roman army was still in camp. In the meantime, Nero marched with a selected corps north and reinforced the Romans there to win the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Metaurus" title="Battle of the Metaurus">
        Battle of the Metaurus
       </a>
       , killing
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hasdrubal_(Barcid)" title="Hasdrubal (Barcid)">
        Hasdrubal
       </a>
       and scattering the survivors of his army. The Carthaginian force under Hasdrubal had left Iberia a year before, after the defeat at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Baecula" title="Battle of Baecula">
        Battle of Baecula
       </a>
       and had been reinforced by Gallic and Ligurian mercenaries and allies. It is notable that they took the same route as Hannibal 10 years previously, but suffered fewer casualties, being better supported by mercenaries from the mountain tribes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011290_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoyos2011290-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Naval_raids_and_expeditions_2">
        Naval raids and expeditions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
